---

## Iter-21 Research Additions (2026-05-09)

Capability-extension delta. Two-track focus: (a) **dataset ingestion** — auxiliary debloat / privacy datasets to make Finder, Debloater, and the Tracker tab smarter without re-deriving them per-device, and (b) **modern Android 14–16 platform APIs** that expose privacy / security signals we currently can't show. Companion research at [`docs/research/2026-05-09-capability-extension.md`](docs/research/2026-05-09-capability-extension.md). Each row is net-new versus iter-18/19/20 and the existing T1–T21 themes. Rows are deliberately scoped to *new data sources* and *unexploited APIs* — capability rows already named in T9 / T16 / T19 (tracker AppOps, Insular cloning, corpse-finder) are not duplicated here.

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **Ingest UAD-NG `uad_lists.json` Dependency Graph** | UAD-NG's `resources/assets/uad_lists.json` ([S212]) populates `dependencies` and `neededBy` densely (~80% of system entries) where our upstream MuntashirAkon dataset populates them sparsely. Add `tools/import_uad.py` that emits a sidecar `dependencies.json` keyed by package id with edges only — don't merge entry bodies (overlap is messy and our descriptions are higher-quality). Refresh weekly via CI. Powers honest "removing X will break Y, Z, W" warnings in the Debloater that today require manual graph authoring. License: GPL-3.0 → AGPL-3.0 one-way OK per FSF. Effort 2/5. | T7 | **Next** |
| **Ingest UAD-NG Preinstalled-Lists for OEM Provenance** | Sister repo `Universal-Debloater-Alliance/universal-android-preinstalled-lists` ([S213]) is a per-OEM ground-truth corpus of "package X is known preinstalled on OEM Y, model Z, region R" claims. Bundle as sidecar `preinstalled.json`, expose via `IFilterableAppInfo.getKnownPreinstallOems()` and surface as Finder filter chips ("preinstalled on Samsung / Pixel / OnePlus / Xiaomi / Motorola") plus an App Info "Provenance" row. Avoids re-deriving the OEM presence map per-device audit. License: GPL-3.0. Effort 2/5. | T7 | **Next** |
| **Ingest IzzyOnDroid `apkscanner-data` SDK Signatures** | `codeberg.org/Katastima/apkscanner-data` ([S214]) ships SDK / NLP / anti-feature signatures that complement the εxodus tracker DB; powers F-Droid IzzyOnDroid antifeature flags. Catches signatures Exodus doesn't (~30–40% additional library coverage on a typical Play Store APK). The existing tracker-scan engine already does regex-match against class-signature lists — adding apkscanner-data is one new asset file + one merged scan pass + dual-source attribution in the Trackers tab. License: GPL-2.0 → GPL-3.0+ compatible. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| ~~**Achno Samsung Debloat List Cross-Check**~~ ✅ audit-clean 2026-05-17 | Audit at [`docs/audits/2026-05-17-achno-samsung-debloat-cross-check.md`](docs/audits/2026-05-17-achno-samsung-debloat-cross-check.md). The one-time sweep extracted 82 unique package-like tokens from `Achno/debloat-samsung-ADB-shizuku` ([S215]); 76 already resolve in the combined local debloat lists. The six exact misses were not added: five are apparent typos or a non-package activity name already covered by nearby Samsung package IDs (`beaconmanager`, `fmm`, `voc`, avatar stickers, Galaxy Essentials widget), and `com.samsung.providers.calendar` has no independent corroboration beyond Achno while local data already covers Samsung Calendar plus AOSP calendar-provider storage. No data mutation shipped. | T7 | ~~**Now**~~ ✅ **audit-clean 2026-05-17** |
| **SDK Sandbox Runtime Enumeration** | Android 14+ `SdkSandboxManager.getSandboxedSdks()` ([S216]) returns the list of advertising / analytics SDKs an app currently has loaded into its sandbox process. Today we detect SDKs at static-analysis time via Exodus signatures; the SDK Runtime surface tells us which sandboxed SDKs are *actually loaded right now*. Add a new "SDK Sandbox" row in App Info → Trackers tab; falls back to "Not supported on this device" below API 34. Adds a runtime-truth column to the static tracker panel. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Domain Verification Audit + Deep-Link Conflict Finder** | `DomainVerificationManager.getDomainVerificationUserState(packageName)` ([S217]) lets us enumerate every domain an app claims via `<intent-filter android:autoVerify="true">`, the verification state per domain (verified / declined / unverified), and — by cross-referencing across all installed apps — which other installed apps claim the same domain. Net effect: a deep-link hijack inspector. v1 = per-app "Domain Verification" tab in App Info (effort 2/5); v2 = system-wide "Deep Link Conflicts" Finder filter (effort 3/5). API 31+ baseline; behaviour expanded in 34. | T9 | **Next** |
| **App Archiving (Android 15+)** | `PackageInstaller.requestArchive()` / `requestUnarchive()` ([S218]) removes the APK while preserving user data — Hail-adjacent freeze with zero privilege requirement (the platform handles it). Pairs with our existing freeze infrastructure as a third state — Active / Frozen / Archived — and unlocks storage reclaim that freeze can't deliver. New "Archive" action in App Info next to Freeze and Force Stop; new "Archive selected (preserves data)" Batch Operations entry. Effort 2/5. | T19 | **Next** |
| **Memory Tagging Extension (MTE) Status Chip** | Per-app manifest property `android:allowNativeHeapPointerTagging` (effective Android 11+) plus runtime MTE state (Android 14+ Pixel 8+) ([S219]) determine whether an app gets MTE-hardened heap protection. Today the user has no way to see who opted in. Add a new "MTE: enabled / disabled / not supported" chip to the App Info tag cloud — sibling to the iter-18 signing-cert SHA-256 chip. Below API 30 displays "MTE: not supported on this device". Effort 1/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Health Connect Privacy Dashboard** | `HealthConnectClient.getGrantedPermissions()` ([S220]) enumerates which apps read or write fitness / sleep / clinical data via the Android 14 mainline Health Connect store. We currently audit standard permissions and AppOps but treat Health Connect as opaque. New "Privacy Dashboard" entry under Settings (or as a sibling tab under T19 Storage Analysis) listing Health Connect permission grants per app. Differentiator vs. every other Android app manager today. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Credential Manager Audit** | `CredentialManager` + `Settings.ACTION_CREDENTIAL_PROVIDER` ([S221]) lets us enumerate which apps registered passkeys / passwords / federated identity providers. Today the user can see *that* providers exist in system Settings but not which credentials are stored, when, or by whom. Pairs with the Health Connect dashboard as a second "Privacy Dashboard" tab. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| ~~**Restricted Settings Unlock Walkthrough**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | Settings -> Privileges now has a Restricted Settings unlock row backed by [`RestrictedSettingsDiagnostics`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/settings/RestrictedSettingsDiagnostics.java). On Android 13+ it classifies AppManagerNG's install source as trusted-store, likely sideloaded, unknown, or review-recommended, then explains why Accessibility / notification listener / device-admin style toggles may be blocked. The walkthrough opens App info for the package so the user can choose **Allow restricted settings**, and also offers Accessibility settings for the affected AppManagerNG service path; the copy includes the ROM variant where the unlock is exposed by long-pressing the disabled toggle. Mode Doctor reports the same install-source details and fix hint. The detector is intentionally "likely/recommended" rather than absolute because Android exposes install-source metadata, not a public per-app Restricted Settings blocked bit. Reference: [S222]. | T5 | ~~**Now**~~ ✅ **shipped 2026-05-17** |
| **MMRL + LSPosed Module Browser Tab** | Read-only enumeration of `/data/adb/modules/` (Magisk + KernelSU + APatch) and `/data/adb/lspd/` (LSPosed) ([S223]) — parse `module.prop` metadata for each. We already detect the active root provider (iter-7); a "Modules" entry under Privilege Health-Check is one tab away. v1 read-only (effort 3/5); v2 toggle modules (effort 3/5); v3 install/upload (effort 4/5). Surfaces module management without requiring users to leave NG for MMRL or LSPosed Manager. | T5 | **Later** |
| **Decision-Logged: Local-VPN Per-App Firewall** | NetGuard / TrackerControl-style local VpnService + DNS proxy + per-app rules ([S224]). Effort 5/5. The biggest single capability gap vs. dedicated tracker-blocking apps. Decision: **park under Under Consideration until T9 AppOps-based tracker blocking has shipped.** Once we have user feedback on whether AppOp-layer enforcement is sufficient, revisit. AppOp blocking is fraction-of-the-cost and addresses the Day-1 user need; a VPN service is a substantially larger surface (battery, MTU, DNS pinning, per-network rules, single-VPN-slot conflict with WireGuard / Mullvad / corporate VPN). Effort 5/5. | T9 | **Under Consideration** |

---

## Iter-22 Research Additions (2026-05-09)

Same-day phase-2 extension after iter-21. Where iter-21 covered datasets and modern Android APIs, iter-22 covers the **operational layer** AppManagerNG hasn't yet built out: privileged-action accountability, recoverability when shells die, automation surfaces (Tasker / QS / Wear), non-phone form factors, localization tooling, migration paths in/out, and offline resilience. Companion research at [`docs/research/2026-05-09-roadmap-extension-phase-2.md`](docs/research/2026-05-09-roadmap-extension-phase-2.md) and [`docs/research/2026-05-09-observability-testing-audit.md`](docs/research/2026-05-09-observability-testing-audit.md). Mandatory category sweep: every prompt-stipulated category (security, accessibility, i18n/l10n, observability, testing, docs, distribution, plugin ecosystem, mobile/non-phone, offline/resilience, multi-user/collab, migration, upgrade) is represented below or already covered in T1–T21 / iter-18–21.

### Reliability & Recoverability

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| ~~**Privileged-Shell Journal + DeathRecipient Replay**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | `BatchOpsJournal` now writes persistent intent/executing state before each `BatchOpsService` run and clears only after `BatchOpsManager.performOp(...)` completes. If the service dies, the process is killed, or Shizuku/Sui's binder-dead callback fires while a batch is active, the journal remains/marks interrupted. `MainActivity` checks the journal on reattach when no batch service is currently working and shows an "Interrupted batch operation" recovery dialog with retry, not-now, and clear actions. The retry path restarts the saved `BatchQueueItem`; normal per-package failures still use the existing failed-app retry flow. Root/ADB LocalServer failures are covered by the persisted executing journal and exception path rather than a fragile socket poll. References: [S225], [S330]. | T5 | **Now** |
| ~~**Mode Self-Test "Doctor"**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | Settings -> Privileges now has a distinct "Mode doctor" active probe beside the passive health rows. It generates a copyable report with ordered PASS/WARN/FAIL/SKIP probes for configured/inferred mode, root binary/grant, root manager and Sui marker, Shizuku binder/UserService/permission/UID, ADB USB/wireless/pairing reachability, LocalServer `id -u`, SELinux domain, and ABI state. Each row includes concrete fix guidance such as granting root, starting/authorizing Shizuku, enabling USB/Wireless debugging, or sharing the support-info bundle after LocalServer failure. References: [S226], [S227]. | T4 | **Now** |
| ~~**LocalServer Bootstrap Smoke Test**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | Settings -> Privileges -> "LocalServer bootstrap smoke test" now runs the LocalServer privileged-shell handshake end-to-end against the current mode, probes `id -u`, and displays a copyable single-line signature on success or failure. The existing bootstrap-failure log path now uses the same `LocalServer.buildBootstrapSignature(...)` formatter, so success and failure reports share device/build/mode/UID/LineageOS/exception/probe fields. Extends the bootstrap-failure-signature feature already shipped in v0.4.1. Reference: [S228]. | T4 | **Now** |
| ~~**Support Info Bundle Composer**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | Settings -> Troubleshooting -> "Share support info" now snapshots Android/ROM build, root/Shizuku/Sui/provider state, AppManagerNG mode, feature flags, the remembered LocalServer bootstrap signature, and the last 120 lines of logcat into a zero-network `support-info-<device>-<ts>.txt` file shared through the system chooser. UIDs are masked, package-like tokens / URIs / paths / emails are scrubbed from the log tail, and no installed-package list is included. References: [S229], [S230]. | T4 | **Now** |
| ~~**Privileged Op Audit Log**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 | The roadmap gap was stale after the earlier op-history implementation: `op_history` is already a Room-backed append-only table with `time`, `type`, `data`, `status`, and metadata `extra`; `OpHistoryActivity` already provides viewer/search/filter/sort/delete/rerun/share, JSON/CSV/text export, and Settings -> Privacy retention controls. Iter-45 completed the explicit `(exit_code, signature)` fields by adding normalized `exit_code` metadata for batch/profile success/failure and platform installer status codes, plus the remembered LocalServer bootstrap signature in details and JSON/CSV export. Current journaled surfaces cover batch ops, installer sessions, and profile runs; per-command shell replay remains the separate Privileged-Shell Journal row. References: [S231], [S232]. | T9 | **Now** |
| **"Was It Me?" Reverse Audit** | Given a package, show every privileged op AppManagerNG performed against it from the audit log. Useful when something broke and the user wonders if AM did it. Power-user accountability; nothing comparable in upstream AM or peers. Composes on top of Privileged Op Audit Log. Effort 2/5. Reference: composes [S231]. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Bundled-Data Freshness Banner + Air-Gap Toggle** | Two-part: (a) write `defs_updated_at` to prefs, banner at >30d, blocking warn at >180d so users don't trust a stale debloat verdict; (b) `prefs.networkDisabled` short-circuits every `OkHttpClient.newCall()` with `IOException("airgap")`. Fails closed; pairs with bundled-only debloat defs for users who refuse network calls. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S233]. | T7 | **Next** |
| **Multi-Mirror Debloat-Defs Fetcher** ⏸ blocked-on-deployment (iter-88 audit) | The source-side prerequisite for multi-mirror is in place: iter-32's `DebloatDefinitionsUpdater` already enforces byte-length + SHA-256 + schema validation on every download, and the host allowlist (`isApprovedRawGithubUrl`) is a one-call validation point that a second-mirror branch could trivially fan out from. **The blocker is operational, not code-side**: a secondary mirror has to actually exist (the project is only hosted on github.com/SysAdminDoc/AppManagerNG; there is no Codeberg / IPFS / mirror endpoint yet). Adding a mirror-iteration loop now would either point at a non-existent URL (hallucination) or ship a one-entry list that pretends to be multi-mirror. The separate **signed manifest** half requires a public-key-in-app + maintainer-signing-pipeline that is a larger eng-debt item; integrity is already enforced by the SHA-256 inside the manifest (which is fetched from the same mirror — so a hostile mirror could substitute both the manifest and the files). Park the row until either (a) a secondary mirror is set up, or (b) the signed-manifest infrastructure lands. Reference: [S234], [S235]. | T7 | **Blocked** |
| **Battery-Aware JobScheduler for Batch Ops** | `setRequiresBatteryNotLow(true)` + `setRequiresDeviceIdle(true)` for non-urgent batch freezes / disables / debloat-passes. Defers to charging-idle windows; respects Doze + App Standby Buckets + Android 16 JobScheduler quotas (already surfaced in iter-18). Effort 2/5. Reference: [S236]. | T6 | **Next** |
| **Atomic-Write Profile Dir + Syncthing Conflict Picker** | Atomic JSON writes with mtime preservation in `/sdcard/AppManagerNG/profiles/` so Syncthing handles peer sync without conflicts; AM-NG ships a conflict-file picker UI for `<name>.sync-conflict-<date>-<peer>.json` files Syncthing emits. Zero-code P2P profile sync. Effort 2/5 (UI only). Reference: [S237]. | T8 | **Next** |

### Migration & Distribution

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| ~~**Snapshot Bundle Export/Import**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 (iter-64) | New `snapshot/SnapshotBundle` writes a ZIP of `shared_prefs/*.xml` (minus `keystore.xml`), `files/profiles/*.am.json`, optional `files/tags/*` (forward-compat for the Multi-Tag row), and the op-history audit log serialized as JSON (`op_history.json`, portable across applicationId rename instead of bundling the raw `apps.db`). Framed by a `manifest.json` with `schema_version=1`, `format=appmanagerng-snapshot`, source package / version / device labels, contents list, per-section counts, and an `excluded` list naming `keystore`. Importer is hardened against path traversal (rejects `..`, slashes, backslashes, ASCII controls in entry names), bounds entry size at 64 MB, refuses bundles with an unknown `format` or a future `schema_version`, and appends op-history rows additively rather than truncating the table. Wired into Settings → Privacy as two prefs (`snapshot_export` via `CreateDocument(application/zip)` and `snapshot_import` via `OpenDocument`); confirm-dialog before import. Pure-JVM coverage: [`SnapshotBundleTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/snapshot/SnapshotBundleTest.java). Reference: [S238]. | T11 | **Now (shipped)** |
| ~~**Importers: Canta + UAD-NG + Hail**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 (iter-65) | New `profiles/importers/ExternalProfileImporter` parses all three formats and content-detects which one each file is. Canta: accepts `{"packages":[…]}`, `{"apps":[…]}`, bare JSON arrays, and `{"data":{"packages":[…]}}` nested-data shapes. UAD-NG: recursively walks every JSON value in `uad_settings.json` and harvests strings matching the Android package-name pattern (defensive against schema drift between point releases). Hail: line-oriented, strips comments (`#…`) and trailing tag flags after the first whitespace or pipe. All three dedupe in insertion order. Hooked into the **Profiles** screen as a new overflow item "Import from Canta / UAD-NG / Hail…" backed by `OpenDocument`; the harvested package list lands as a fresh `AppsProfile` via the existing `BaseProfile.newProfile` factory and opens the profile editor for review. Pure-JVM coverage: [`ExternalProfileImporterTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/profiles/importers/ExternalProfileImporterTest.java). References: [S239], [S240], [S241]. | T8 | **Next (shipped)** |
| ~~**Export-to-Upstream-AM Compat Profile**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 (iter-66) | New `profiles/importers/UpstreamCompatProfileExporter` emits a strict allowlist subset of NG's serialised profile JSON, keyed to the upstream `BaseProfile` / `AppsBaseProfile` / `AppsProfile` schema as of the NG bootstrap commit (`3d11bcb`). Any NG-only field that later gets added must explicitly opt in to compat export by joining the allowlist — the default is to drop it silently rather than risk a half-broken file. Filter-based profiles (NG-only `PROFILE_TYPE_APPS_FILTER`) are refused with a typed `UpstreamCompatExportException` and a user-facing explainer toast. Wired into the per-profile popup as a new "Export for upstream App Manager" action that writes `<profile>.upstream-am.json` via `CreateDocument`. Pure-JVM coverage: [`UpstreamCompatProfileExporterTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/profiles/importers/UpstreamCompatProfileExporterTest.java) — allowlist enumeration is locked down so unintended schema drift is a test failure. Reference: [S01]. | T11 | **Next (shipped)** |
| **WebDAV Snapshot Target** | DAV4JVM-backed WebDAV destination for the snapshot bundle (#export-import). Hits the Nextcloud / ownCloud / Hetzner Storage Box use case the way Aegis does for vault sync. Effort 3/5. Reference: [S242]. | T6 | **Later** |
| ~~**APK Share-Target Receiver**~~ ✅ 2026-05-17 (stale gap closed by audit) | Already implemented in the installer surface: [`PackageInstallerActivity`](app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml) is exported for `ACTION_SEND` with `application/vnd.android.package-archive`, `application/vnd.apkm`, `application/xapk-package-archive`, and `application/octet-stream`; it also accepts `ACTION_SEND_MULTIPLE` and `ACTION_VIEW` / `ACTION_INSTALL_PACKAGE` for `file:`, `content:`, and `package:` URIs. [`ApkQueueItem.fromIntent()`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/ApkQueueItem.java) consumes the shared URIs and persists granted URI permission when available. [`PackageInstallerActivity`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/PackageInstallerActivity.java) then shows tracker counts, dependency warnings, checksum confirmation, and signature-mismatch handling before or during the install flow. Reference: [S243]. | T11 | **Now** |
| ~~**`floss` vs `full` Build Flavors (F-Droid Clean Path)**~~ ✅ 2026-05-17 | `app/build.gradle` now defines the `distribution` flavor dimension with default `floss` (`BuildConfig.ALLOW_OPTIONAL_NETWORK_FEATURES=false`) and `full` (`true`). `floss` preserves local ADB/localhost networking but disables the optional user-facing Internet feature gate, VirusTotal/Pithus scan-report lookups, and debloat-definition auto-update path through `FeatureController`; `full` keeps those surfaces available behind the existing opt-in settings. Release reproducibility scripts collect recursive flavored APK outputs, CI artifact globs cover flavored unit/lint reports, Obtainium now filters for `full` assets, and [`docs/distribution/build-flavors.md`](docs/distribution/build-flavors.md) pins F-Droid metadata to `flossRelease` with F-Droid anti-feature rationale. Reference: [S244], [S245]. | T1 | **Now** |

### Automation Surface (T8 deepening)

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| ~~**Broadcast Intent API (`io.github.sysadmindoc.AppManagerNG.action.*`)**~~ ✅ 2026-05-17 | Concrete schema for the existing T8 placeholder is shipped in [`AutomationIntents`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/automation/AutomationIntents.java) and [`AutomationReceiver`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/automation/AutomationReceiver.java). The manifest declares `io.github.sysadmindoc.AppManagerNG.permission.AUTOMATION` as `signature` and requires it on the exported receiver. Supported actions cover `FREEZE` / `UNFREEZE` / `FORCE_STOP` / `CLEAR_CACHE` / `CLEAR_DATA` / `UNINSTALL` / `BACKUP` / `RESTORE` / `DISABLE_COMPONENT` / `ENABLE_COMPONENT` / `RUN_PROFILE` / `INSTALL_FROM_URI` / `SCAN_TRACKERS`, routing service work through existing batch/profile/installer/app-details paths. Full contract documented in [`docs/intent-api.md`](docs/intent-api.md). Reference: [S246], [S247]. | T8 | **Now** |
| ~~**`am://` URI Scheme — Concrete Schema**~~ ✅ 2026-05-09 (App Info alias shipped, freeze/profile/install deferred) | First concrete shape of the schema documented at [`docs/intent-api.md`](docs/intent-api.md). **`am://app/<pkg>?user=<uid>` shipped** as a short alias for the canonical `app-manager://details?id=<pkg>&user=<uid>`: new `AM_SCHEME` + `APP_HOST` constants in [`SelfUriManager`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/self/SelfUriManager.java), parsing routes through the existing `getUserPackagePairFromUri()` so consumers don't change; new intent-filter `<data android:host="app" android:scheme="am"/>` on the `details.AppInfoActivity` activity-alias in [`AndroidManifest.xml`](app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml). The remaining shapes (`am://freeze/<pkg>`, `am://profile/<id>/run`, `am://install?source=<url>`) are reserved in the docs but **not yet wired** — they need the iter-22 T8 broadcast-intent automation surface ([S247]) for the authorization model (signature-permission-gated callers vs. user-confirmed dialogs). Pairs with T18 deep-link infrastructure — same URL-dispatch layer. Reference: [S246]. | T8 | **Now** |
| **Tasker Plugin (In-App, No Separate APK)** | Add `com.twofortyfouram.locale.intent.action.EDIT_SETTING` activity + `FIRE_SETTING` receiver inside NG. Pulls in `com.joaomgcd:taskerpluginlibrary` (~120 KB APK growth). Action plugin only (no event/state/condition v2 in v1). Works with Automate (LlamaLab) + MacroDroid for free — both consume Locale-spec plugins. **Novelty 5/5 in the AM/Canta/Hail/SD Maid/Neo Backup space**: SD Maid has had open Tasker tickets for ~7 years; AM has [#1219](https://github.com/MuntashirAkon/AppManager/issues/1219) closed-as-duplicate. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S248], [S249], [S250]. | T8 | **Next** |
| **Per-App Pinned QS TileService** | `TileService` bound to a single user-pinned app for repeat force-stop on a misbehaving app. Distinct from the iter-18 "Hail-Style Auto-Freeze QuickSettings Tile" (which runs a profile); this tile is per-app force-stop. Use Android 13's `TileService.requestAddTileService()` for one-tap install from onboarding. Effort 1/5. Reference: [S251]. | T8 | **Next** |
| ~~**App Shortcut: Freeze / Force-Stop / Clear Cache Per-App**~~ ✅ 2026-05-17 | [`AppActionShortcutPublisher`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/shortcut/AppActionShortcutPublisher.java) publishes dynamic launcher shortcuts from the loaded app list, choosing recent installed packages and only exposing actions supported by the current privilege path: freeze, force-stop, and clear-cache. [`AppActionShortcutActivity`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/shortcut/AppActionShortcutActivity.java) is non-exported, runs after normal `BaseActivity` authentication, and dispatches through the same `FreezeUtils` / `PackageManagerCompat` helpers as App Details. [`AppInfoFragment`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/details/info/AppInfoFragment.java) now lets users pin force-stop and clear-cache action shortcuts by long-pressing those action chips, and freeze shortcuts default to "Freeze <app>" / "Unfreeze <app>" labels. Unit coverage: [`AppActionShortcutPublisherTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/shortcut/AppActionShortcutPublisherTest.java). Reference: [S252]. | T8 | **Now** |
| **Sharing Shortcuts API for Direct-Share** | Publish top-N apps as direct-share targets so a user can send a backup / profile JSON straight to a contact-shaped target. Replaces deprecated `ChooserTargetService` (gone in SDK 31). Effort 2/5. Reference: [S253]. | T11 | **Later** |
| **DocumentsProvider for `am://backups` + `am://profiles`** | Backups + profile JSONs surface in any SAF picker (Files by Google, Material Files, Solid Explorer). `MANAGE_DOCUMENTS` not required since paths are user-scoped. Backup managers don't ship this — high differentiation. Effort 3/5. Reference: [S254]. | T6 | **Later** |
| ~~**Assist App Handler / Quick Pick**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-18 (iter-119) | Closed by the Hail-style Digital Assistant implementation above: `android.intent.action.ASSIST` now lands in the dedicated quick-action sheet, resolves the foreground package from assist extras or recent usage events, exposes Force Stop / Freeze / Open App Details, and offers Running Apps as the no-target recovery path. Reference: [S130]. | T8 | **Shipped** |

### Form-Factor Expansion (T17 + new themes)

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **`ListDetailPaneScaffold` + 5-Breakpoint WindowSizeClass** | Concretize T17 Adaptive Layout. Use Jetpack WindowManager 1.4 + `androidx.compose.material3.adaptive.ListDetailPaneScaffold` driven off `currentWindowAdaptiveInfo().windowSizeClass`. Five M3 breakpoints: Compact / Medium / Expanded / Large / XL (TriFold / Tab S11 Ultra / external display). Without this, NG looks dated on a Tab S11 vs. Inure / Material Files. Note: NG ships Views, not Compose — the equivalent is `SlidingPaneLayout` + `WindowMetricsCalculator` + `WindowInfoTracker`; same UX shape, different API. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S255], [S256], [S257]. | T17 | **Next** |
| **Foldable Posture Awareness** | `WindowInfoTracker.windowLayoutInfo` → `FoldingFeature` (state FLAT / HALF_OPENED, orientation, isSeparating) plus WindowManager 1.4's `supportedPostures` API for tabletop detection. Z Fold 7 / Pixel Fold 2 use case: package list on outer panel, detail on inner panel when unfolded. Zero net-new effort once master/detail row above lands — Activity Embedding handles fold/unfold transitions for free. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S258]. | T17 | **Next** |
| **DeX Multi-Instance + Pop-Up Resizeable** | `Intent.FLAG_ACTIVITY_LAUNCH_ADJACENT \| NEW_TASK \| MULTIPLE_TASK` to allow two NG instances side-by-side (compare two app's manifests, diff permissions). One UI 8 / Android 16 introduced new pop-up swipe handle on Z TriFold and tablets — declare `android:resizeableActivity="true"` and support `android.allow_multiple_resumed_activities`. Free win. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S259]. | T8 | **Later** |
| **ChromeOS ARCVM Detection + UX Polish** | `hasSystemFeature("org.chromium.arc.device_management")` → hide phone-only ops (SIM, telephony bloat), surface ChromeOS-broker constraints (system installs go through ChromeOS, not `pm`). Keyboard / mouse polish piggybacks on master/detail. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S260]. | T17 | **Later** |
| **Android XR Manifest + Spatial Track** | `<uses-feature android:name="android.software.xr.api.spatial" android:required="false"/>` plus optional XR-track variant on Play (`android.software.xr.api.openxr`) sharing the same package name. Galaxy XR launches Q4 2026 with **the most open sideload story of any XR platform** — direct APK install from browser, no PC, no developer mode. Lands NG as plausibly the first FOSS app manager on Android XR. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S261], [S262]. | T1 | **Later** |
| **Wear OS Phone-Side Companion** | The killer addition. **No FOSS app does this.** Phone-side ADB-over-WiFi to paired Wear OS watch, `WearableListenerService` + `MessageClient` for live state, ~200 KB companion APK on the watch with same package ID + signing cert. Operations: list packages, pull APK, disable / enable, force-stop, clear data, `pm uninstall --user 0`, set DPI, debloat with red/orange/green safety scoring. Galaxy Watch 7+ uses One UI Watch 6 + Wear OS 5; bootloader locked but `pm` works fine. Effort 4/5. Defer until [`Wear OS Tiles + Material3TileService`](https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/tiles/versioning) infrastructure stabilizes; under-consideration not because of risk but because of effort + bandwidth. Reference: [S263], [S264], [S265]. | T16 | **Under Consideration** |

### Localization & i18n

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **Hosted Weblate Bridge (NewPipe / Tachiyomi Pattern)** | Bridge to upstream's `hosted.weblate.org/projects/app-manager/` as a separate `app-manager-ng` component sharing upstream's glossary + TM. Cost ~1 day setup, free hosting. Win: every locale upstream gains flows downstream, NG-specific strings (Pro mode, M3 dashboard labels) translate independently. Self-hosted Weblate is overkill at this scale; Crowdin OSS reintroduces a proprietary dep. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S266], [S267]. | T10 | **Now** |
| ~~**Pseudolocale Build Variants + RTL CI Pass**~~ ✅ 2026-05-09 (build-side) | `pseudoLocalesEnabled true` set on the `debug` build type in [`app/build.gradle`](app/build.gradle); release stays clean. Debug builds now bake `en-XA` (accented + bracketed text — catches truncation, missing-translatable strings) and `en-XB` (RTL mirror of English — catches RTL layout breaks). Activate via `adb shell setprop persist.sys.locale en-XA` (or via Settings → Developer options → Pseudolocale on Android 13+). The CI screenshot-diff side of this row (`connectedCheck` matrix + PR comment) stays open as a follow-up — gates on the **Espresso + UI Automator Smoke Pack** row landing first (it provides the headless instrumentation pipe the screenshot capture needs). Reference: [S268]. | T10 | **Next** |
| ~~**Per-App Locale Picker (`AppCompatDelegate.setApplicationLocales`)**~~ ✅ 2026-05-09 | Wired the in-app language preference into the OS-side per-app locale: [`Prefs.Appearance.setLanguage()`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/settings/Prefs.java) now calls `AppCompatDelegate.setApplicationLocales(LocaleListCompat)` after persisting the preference, and registers `androidx.appcompat.app.AppLocalesMetadataHolderService` (`autoStoreLocales=true`, `enabled=false`) in [`AndroidManifest.xml`](app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml) for API 26-32 SharedPreferences-backed back-port. `android:localeConfig="@xml/locales_config"` was already declared at the application level, so on API 33+ the OS surfaces AM-NG in **Settings → Apps → AppManagerNG → Language** out of the box; the new wiring keeps that surface in sync with the in-app picker bidirectionally. `LANG_AUTO` maps to `LocaleListCompat.getEmptyLocaleList()` so "Auto" tracks the system locale via the platform mechanism rather than NG's own override pipeline. The existing `AppearanceUtils.applyConfigurationChangesToActivities()` recreate path remains untouched and continues to drive immediate in-app re-render. Reference: [S269]. | T10 | **Now** |

### Observability + Testing + CI

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **In-App Log Viewer with Severity Filter + Redaction** | Replace raw logcat surface with structured viewer: filter by tag / severity, one-tap "redact UIDs / paths / package names" for screenshot sharing, "copy line" button. Inure ships this. Protects users when pasting into issues. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S270]. | T4 | **Next** |
| **Opt-In Local ACRA-Style Crash Sink** | ACRA configured to write crash reports to `Documents/AppManagerNG/crashes/*.json`, NOT a network endpoint. User shares via Support Info Bundle Composer. Default OFF. F-Droid `Tracking` antifeature avoided because no network and disabled by default. Effort 2/5. Reference: [S271], [S244]. | T4 | **Under Consideration** |
| **Macrobenchmark Module + Baseline Profiles** | New `:benchmark` module measuring cold-start, package-list scroll jank, Backups screen TTI. Run on physical device in CI nightly; results posted as PR comment. Generate Baseline Profile for the app-list path. AM cold-start is dominated by `PackageManager` enumeration — exactly the workload where Baseline Profiles deliver outsized win. Pure local, no privacy cost. Effort 4/5. Reference: [S272]. | T20 | **Later** |
| **Espresso + UI Automator Smoke Pack** | Headless device-side suite that exercises: open app-list, freeze / unfreeze test package, view component blocker, run one-shot rule. Runs in `connectedCheck` on emulator matrix (API 26 / 30 / 34 / 35 / 36). SD Maid SE ships these; AM has zero. Catches regressions in privileged ops without user telemetry. Note: this is a *smoke pack for power-user flows*, distinct from the project's "no unit tests unless requested" policy in `CLAUDE.md`. Effort 4/5. Reference: [S273]. | T11 | **Later** |
| ~~**CI Dependency CVE Scan**~~ ✅ 2026-05-09 | Two-layer pipeline shipped at [`.github/workflows/dependency-scan.yml`](.github/workflows/dependency-scan.yml): (a) **PR Dependency Review** runs `actions/dependency-review-action@v4` on every pull request, fails the PR on HIGH/CRITICAL severity introduced by a dependency change and denies CC-BY-NC* / CC-BY-ND* / AGPL-1.0 licenses up-front (GPL-3.0-or-later compatibility); (b) **Weekly OWASP Dependency Check** (`org.owasp:dependency-check-gradle:10.0.3`, classpath in [`build.gradle`](build.gradle)) on Sunday 04:13 UTC + manual `workflow_dispatch` produces a full HTML/SARIF report uploaded as artifact (catches CVEs disclosed *after* the dependency landed). Configured to consume an `NVD_API_KEY` secret when set for higher rate limits, anonymous fallback otherwise. Local runs use `failBuildOnCVSS = 11.0` (effectively never fail) so the report is purely informational; CI uses `continue-on-error: true` and surfaces the report rather than failing the entire weekly cadence on a single new CVE. F-Droid reproducible-build pipeline already does signature checks; this stacks the CVE check on top. Reference: [S274]. | T4 | **Now** |
| **OEM Quirk Panel** | Detect Samsung Knox / MIUI / EMUI / OxygenOS / ColorOS / OneUI / HyperOS at runtime. Surface known limitations (Knox container packages can't be frozen; MIUI auto-restarts disabled apps; EMUI revokes notification access; HyperOS aggressive App Standby). Link to per-OEM workaround page in app. UAD-NG carries per-OEM lists; AM users hit these constantly. Effort 3/5. Reference: [S275], [S240]. | T9 | **Next** |

### Plugin Ecosystem

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **MMRL System-App Distribution Channel** | Ship NG as a `signature \| privileged` system-app via MMRL's Magisk / KernelSU / APatch module repo so it can use platform-signature-gated APIs without manual `/system` install. NG already detects all four root managers (iter-7). Module repo URL pinned, signed, optional install path. Effort 3/5. Reference: [S276]. | T1 | **Later** |
| **LSPosed Companion Module** | Optional `am-xposed-helpers` module — auto-unfreeze on launch (Hail just shipped this), bypass component-blocking on whitelisted apps, log hidden API calls for the Audit Log. NG core stays Xposed-free — ships as a separate module APK. Effort 4/5. Reference: [S277]. | T9 | **Under Consideration** |
| **KDE Connect Plugin (Custom `packetType`)** | New `packetType: kdeconnect.appmanager.action` so desktop KDE Connect can trigger freeze / uninstall / backup-now on phone. Submit upstream PR; ship pre-built fork as fallback. Cross-device power-user surface no AM-class app has. Effort 4/5. Reference: [S278]. | T8 | **Under Consideration** |
| **Termux:API-Style Helper APK** | `com.sysadmindoc.appmanagerng.shell` companion APK exposes `am-shell freeze <pkg>` from Termux. Unix-socket dispatcher pattern from `TermuxApiReceiver`. Optional install. Effort 4/5. Reference: [S279]. | T8 | **Under Consideration** |

### Rejects (with reasoning)

| Item | Reasoning |
|------|-----------|
| **Android Automotive OS package management** | AAOS apps are restricted to media / nav / messaging / parking / charging / IoT / weather templates. Power-user package management is not a sanctioned category. AOSP's `disable_packages` doc is for OEMs building the OS, not third-party tools. Effort 5+, differentiation 0. Reference: [S280]. |
| **Android Auto projection** | No package management surface. Car App Library is template-only. |
| **Wear OS standalone Tile / Complication for managing watch from watch** | Novelty without value — power-user watch management belongs on the phone. The phone-side Wear OS companion (above) is the right shape. |
| **Firebase Analytics / Crashlytics / Performance** | Triggers F-Droid `Tracking` + `NonFreeNet` antifeatures, requires GMS, defeats the AM-class user demographic. |
| **Always-on cloud Sentry (any deployment)** | Even with `sendDefaultPii=false` + `beforeSend` scrubber, AM stack traces leak target package names = user behaviour. F-Droid still flags. Acceptable only as **opt-in + self-hosted + scrubber** — already expressed via the Local ACRA Crash Sink under-consideration row. |
| **Anonymous feature-usage counters** | F-Droid's Tracking rule is bright-line: opt-in default-off only. Any "user opened Permissions tab" counter violates project posture. Reference: [S244]. |
| **Play Console Android Vitals** | Distribution is F-Droid + GitHub Releases + IzzyOnDroid + Accrescent; no Play Console signal exists. |
| **Play Integrity / SafetyNet attestation** | Antithetical to a tool whose users root their devices. |
| **Google Play In-App Update API** | GMS dependency; we ship update checks via GitHub Releases JSON / Obtainium / F-Droid's own update channels. |
| **Crowdin OSS plan** | Plausible alternative to Weblate, but reintroduces a proprietary dependency a GPL fork shouldn't accept when Weblate Libre exists and upstream already uses it. Reference: [S266]. |
| **Self-hosted Weblate** | Overkill until contributor count >50 or upstream relationship breaks. Reference: [S266]. |
| **Tor onion mirror for debloat-defs** | Niche; only matters if AM-NG ever becomes geo-blocked. Premature. |
| **Google Drive sync (REST API)** | OAuth + Play Services; conflicts with FOSS-pure positioning. WebDAV (above) covers the use case without Play Services. |

---

## Iter-23 Repo Reconciliation + 2026 Platform Delta (2026-05-16)

Phase-0 state memo: AppManagerNG is an Android power-user package manager fork, not a generic app store or desktop debloater. The current repo is Java/Kotlin Android Views + Material Components, Gradle/AGP, GPL-3.0-or-later, minSdk 21, targetSdk 36, release 0.4.2 / versionCode 6. Its stated philosophy is "retain upstream App Manager power, remove friction": progressive disclosure, rootless/Shizuku/ADB first, no Compose migration yet, no telemetry by default, and no cloud/account dependency for core workflows. Local reconnaissance found the shipped source largely consistent with that philosophy, but several roadmap/docs claims have drifted from disk: `README.md` and the old roadmap claim an NG-specific `CONTRIBUTING.md` exists when it does not; release docs advertise ABI choices while `release.yml` uploads only the universal APK; lint/tests workflows do not trigger for the actual `main` branch; and the changelog claims dependency-check `13.1.1` while `versions.gradle` pins `10.0.3`.

External signal snapshot (GitHub/API snapshot 2026-05-16): upstream AM remains the capability reference (8,025 stars, 213 open issues, pushed 2026-04-16 [S291]); Canta (4,780 stars, pushed 2026-05-12 [S292]), UAD-NG (6,606 stars, pushed 2026-05-11 [S293]), Hail (5,821 stars, pushed 2026-04-26 [S294]), Inure (1,757 stars, pushed 2026-05-16 [S295]), SD Maid SE (6,740 stars, pushed 2026-05-16 [S296]), Neo Backup (3,614 stars, pushed 2026-05-03 [S297]), Android-DataBackup (6,690 stars, pushed 2026-05-14 [S298]), Shizuku (25,130 stars [S299]), LibChecker (6,866 stars, pushed 2026-05-16 [S300]), AppVerifier (1,046 stars [S301]), and Obtainium (17,115 stars [S302]) define the active OSS feature envelope. Commercial signal says users still pay for polished backup scheduling/cloud destinations (Swift Backup, Titanium Backup [S305], [S306]), app history/tags/insights (AppDash [S304]), and lower-friction desktop debloat flows (ADB AppControl [S303]). NG should harvest the workflow lessons, not the account-bound or desktop-only architecture.

### Now: Contract Repair Before More Feature Work

Covers per-surface impact (main list, App Details, backup/restore, debloater, profiles, batch ops, scanner, Filters/Finder, logcat), the no-telemetry/no-cloud posture, distribution-channel eligibility (Play deliberately not pursued because of co-declared privileged permissions), and a maintainer gate so future `<uses-permission>` / `<queries>` edits run through the document before shipping. Reference: [S308]. | 3/5 | 1/5 | Low; docs-only unless distribution channels change. | Parity | **Shipped** — justification lives at [`docs/distribution/package-visibility.md`](docs/distribution/package-visibility.md). |

The bug report adds NG-specific support-bundle prompts (active mode, privilege provider, LocalServer bootstrap signature, install source, security patch, ROM/build, architecture, affected operation) so the intake meshes with the future "Support Info Bundle Composer" feature in row 577. The PR template replaces the upstream blanket AI/LLM ban with the tool-assisted-but-reviewed contract from `CONTRIBUTING.md`. References: [S289], [S290]. | 3/5 | 1/5 | Low; future support-bundle composer can extend the same field set. | Parity | **Shipped** — triage intake now collects what AppManagerNG triage actually needs. |

### Next: Feature Harvest That Fits NG

| Candidate | Evidence + fit | Impact | Effort | Risk / dependencies | Novelty | Tier |
|-----------|----------------|--------|--------|---------------------|---------|------|
| ~~**Installer Dependency Resolver**~~ ✅ 2026-05-16 (v1: minSdk gate + `<uses-library>` check) | The long-standing `// TODO: Resolve dependencies` in [`PackageInstallerActivity`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/PackageInstallerActivity.java) is now a real call into the new [`InstallDependencyChecker`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/InstallDependencyChecker.java). v1 covers the two most common silent install failures: `INSTALL_FAILED_OLDER_SDK` (when `applicationInfo.minSdkVersion > Build.VERSION.SDK_INT`) and `INSTALL_FAILED_MISSING_SHARED_LIBRARY` (when an APK declares `<uses-library>` entries the device's `PackageManager.getSystemSharedLibraryNames()` does not advertise). Each detected issue is rendered as a localized line below the existing tracker callout, so users see the block before they tap Install. Helper is Android-API-free; JVM tests in [`InstallDependencyCheckerTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/InstallDependencyCheckerTest.java) cover floor-met / floor-not-met / unknown-version cases plus shared-library dedup / trim / missing-name aggregation. Follow-up rows for ABI compatibility and split-APK base-missing detection can extend the same checker without touching the call site. References: [S314], [S304], [S309]. | 4/5 | 3/5 | Medium; ABI + split-base-missing checks tracked as follow-up extension of the same helper. | Parity | **Shipped** — minSdk + `<uses-library>` checks both surface above the install button; ABI / split follow-ups stay open. |
| ~~**Developer Verification Install Transcript**~~ ✅ 2026-05-16 | Install-failure dialog in [`PackageInstallerActivity`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/PackageInstallerActivity.java) now exposes a "Copy diagnostic info" neutral button on any non-success status. The new [`InstallTranscript`](app/src/main/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/InstallTranscript.java) captures timestamp, AppManagerNG version + code, manufacturer + model + device, Android release + API + security patch, ABI, active Ops mode, package name, status code + name, status message, and the source URI — redacted by default so `file:///storage/...`, `content://provider/document/id`, and `https://host/path` paste safely (scheme + authority kept, path replaced with `<redacted>`). `ApkSource.getUri()` was added (null default, overridden in `UriApkSource` / `CachedApkSource`) so the transcript reads the raw source without leaking it. Pure-JVM tests in [`InstallTranscriptTest`](app/src/test/java/io/github/muntashirakon/AppManager/apk/installer/InstallTranscriptTest.java) cover redaction and stable line ordering. References: [S172], [S173], [S310]. | 4/5 | 2/5 | Medium privacy risk; redaction is on by default, opt-in for verbatim source is a future toggle. | Leapfrog | **Shipped** — install failures now copy a paste-friendly diagnostic block. |
| **App Notes / Tags / Watchlist Layer** | Commercial AppDash monetizes app history, tagging, and install insight workflows ([S304]); NG already has package inventory and profiles. | 3/5 | 2/5 | Low; local SQLite only, no telemetry. | Parity | **Next** — useful once audit-log and Finder work settle. |
| ~~**Backup Destination Capability Matrix**~~ ✅ 2026-05-16 | New [`docs/distribution/backup-destinations.md`](docs/distribution/backup-destinations.md) is the canonical inventory of what backup destinations NG supports today (native primary / adopted / removable / USB-OTG via SAF), which destinations are indirect via third-party DocumentsProvider apps (WebDAV, SMB, FTP/SFTP, cloud via Material Files / DAVx⁵ / FolderSync / RCX), and which ones are deliberately rejected (direct Google Drive / Dropbox / OneDrive OAuth — they fail the no-cloud / no-telemetry contract in `CONTRIBUTING.md`). Documents reliability watch-outs per provider, planned destinations cross-linked to existing roadmap rows (Atomic-Write Profile Dir, Backup Retention, Integrity Verification, Sharing Button, Scheduled Auto-Backup), and a "recommended setup per use case" matrix. References: [S305], [S306]. | 4/5 | 3/5 | Medium; future plug-in/provider work tracked separately under iter-23 "Later". | Parity | **Shipped** — provider posture now lives at [`docs/distribution/backup-destinations.md`](docs/distribution/backup-destinations.md). |
| **F-Droid Index-v2 Metadata Reader (Read-Only)** | F-Droid's modern API exposes package metadata suitable for provenance checks without building a full app store ([S311]). | 3/5 | 3/5 | Low-medium; must stay read-only and avoid duplicating Obtainium/F-Droid clients. | Leapfrog | **Next** — fits as "where did this APK come from?" metadata, not update tracking. |
| **Accessibility + Pseudolocale Screenshot Gate** | Pseudolocales are already enabled for debug builds, but screenshot CI remains deferred; AndroidX/Material minSdk churn makes regression gates more important ([S315], [S268], [S307]). | 3/5 | 3/5 | Medium; depends on the UI Automator smoke pack. | Parity | **Next** — catches layout damage from the premium UI track. |

### Later / Under Consideration

| Candidate | Evidence + fit | Impact | Effort | Risk / dependencies | Novelty | Tier |
|-----------|----------------|--------|--------|---------------------|---------|------|
| **ADB AppControl-Style Desktop Companion** | ADB AppControl proves desktop debloat UX demand ([S303]), but NG's strategy is on-device power tooling. | 2/5 | 5/5 | High maintenance and platform split; depends on a stable remote-command API. | Parity | **Under Consideration** — only revisit after T8 automation/API surfaces are stable. |
| **Commercial Cloud Backup APIs** | Swift/Titanium cloud destinations are a paid differentiator ([S305], [S306]), but OAuth/GMS/account coupling conflicts with FOSS/offline posture. | 3/5 | 4/5 | High privacy/support risk; WebDAV/SAF/Syncthing should land first. | Parity | **Under Consideration** — allow plug-in/provider architecture first, not hard-coded Google Drive. |

Mandatory category self-check for this pass: security (CVE banner, dependency scan, package visibility), accessibility/i18n (pseudolocale gate, Material minSdk), observability/testing (CI repair, issue intake), docs/distribution (governance docs, release artifact matrix), plugin ecosystem (left to existing T8/T9 rows), mobile/offline/resilience (F-Droid metadata read-only, no cloud requirement), multi-user/collab (not expanded; existing Finder multi-user debt remains), migration/upgrade (minSdk ledger, release contract). Thin areas are intentional: multi-user and plugin work already have stronger existing rows than any net-new source found in this pass.

## Iter-25 Research Additions (2026-05-17)

Nine-day delta off iter-23 (closing 2026-05-08): autonomous research-session sweep on competitor releases, Android 17 platform progression, in-flight uncommitted-work audit. Companion artifacts at [`.ai/research/2026-05-17/`](.ai/research/2026-05-17/) and [`.ai/research/2026-05-17-pass-2/`](.ai/research/2026-05-17-pass-2/). The session also stood up [`docs/architecture/`](docs/architecture/) closing T11 "Architecture Documentation" — see §"Iter-25 Closures" below.

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **Shizuku Android-17 Compatibility Watch** | Shizuku 13.6.0 has confirmed Android 17 Beta 3 regressions, but the evidence is mixed: #1965 reports a blank Application Management page while authorized apps still appear to function; #1967 reports broader "app won't get Shizuku" failure; #1988 repeats the Android 17 managed-apps-empty symptom on Pixel 9 Pro XL [S321, S322, S326]. The thedjchi Shizuku fork has an assigned v14.0.0 Android 17 support issue noting new `ACCESS_LOCAL_NETWORK` pairing pressure [S327]. **NG-side mitigation shipped 2026-05-17**: `ShizukuBridge.hasAndroid17CompatibilityRisk(Context)` warns on API 37 while `MIN_ANDROID_17_COMPATIBLE_VERSION` is unknown, onboarding surfaces a Wireless ADB fallback banner, and `.github/workflows/shizuku-release-watch.yml` opens a maintainer issue when Shizuku release notes mention Android 17 / #1965 / #1967. Remaining action: verify on an Android 17 device/image, then populate the fixed-version floor when upstream ships a confirmed fix. Cross-reference iter-19's "Hidden-Shizuku Fork Detection" [S139, S152] in case the community migrates to forks. | T5 | **Watch / mitigated** |
| **Android 17 Stable June 2026 — targetSdk=37 Audit Batch Sequencing** | Android 17 Beta 3 reached platform stability on 2026-03-26; API surface is locked; stable rollout to Pixel devices targets **June 2026** [S324]. The Engineering Debt Register's "Android 17 targetSdk=37 compliance batch" remains the single largest open Eng-Debt item — five open sub-audits (ACCESS_LOCAL_NETWORK runtime permission, usesCleartextTraffic enforcement, MODE_BACKGROUND_ACTIVITY_START_ALLOWED migration, ECH default-on, ML-DSA Keystore OID recognition). Schedule the audit batch into v0.7.x window so the targetSdk bump can land alongside the next minor. Effort cumulative 4/5. | Eng-Debt | **Next** |
| **Neo-Backup 8.3.18 (2026-05-04)** | Minor bump from 8.3.17 cited at iter-18 [S135] / iter-19 [S114]. No NG-action delta surfaced — the rows already derived from 8.3.17 remain accurate. Source-register version pointer updated at [S323]. | T6 | **(no row delta)** |

| **Iter-24 In-Progress Fix Triple (commit-ready, 2026-05-17)** | Three commit-ready in-progress fixes surfaced by the 2026-05-17 research-run uncommitted-work audit, all landed during the iter-25 follow-through: (1) **`fix(finder)`** [73387cd] — `FilterOption.setKeyValue()` was wrapping every regex predicate in `Pattern.quote()`, silently neutering iter-23's tracker-name regex work into literal-string matches; (2) **`security(installer)`** [bcb2874] — install-transcript URI redactor now strips userinfo / query / fragment per RFC 3986 §3.2 (previously leaked `https://host?token=…` and `https://user:pass@host/…` shapes through the "Copy diagnostic info" surface); (3) **`fix(onboarding)`** [25c629a] — root-manager probe captures `Application` context on main thread before background post (`requireContext()` on a detached fragment from a worker pool was silently killing the worker and leaving onboarding root-suffix unpopulated). New `FilterOptionTest` (Robolectric) lands alongside (1). | T7 / T3 / T4 | **Shipped 2026-05-17** |

## Iter-63 Research Additions (2026-05-17 — pass 40)

Forty-pass autonomous research-run extension off iter-62: external sweep on competitor releases shipped in the 2026-05-04 → 2026-05-17 window, dependency-pin currency check, Android platform progression delta, community pain-point mining, and a pass-40 code-side reliability/security audit covering resource leaks, race conditions, and shell-injection defense-in-depth across modules untouched by iter-1 → iter-62. The audit fix set is uncommitted in the working tree at the time of writing; tracked-implementation files are listed in the **Iter-63 Closures** subsection below.

The external sweep deliberately re-checked the **Material Components 1.14.0** ceiling claim, the **AGP** pin, and the **biometric** dependency line because those three are load-bearing for the long-term minSdk-21 → 23 ceiling decision tracked in [`docs/policy/minsdk-21-ceiling.md`](docs/policy/minsdk-21-ceiling.md). All three turned up findings that move the ledger — see "Corrections to existing rows" first.

### Corrections to existing rows

| Item | Correction | Impact | Source |
|------|------------|--------|--------|
| **Material Components 1.14.0** | Iter-25 [S325] recorded "1.14.0 stable has not shipped". Re-verifying upstream releases page on 2026-05-17 shows **1.14.0 stable shipped 2025-05-13** and the line has since progressed through 1.14.0-rc01 (Apr 2025) → 1.14.0 stable (May 2025). The minSdk-23 ceiling decision is **not deferred**; it is the active gate on bumping the Material line. `versions.gradle` line 36 comment ("1.14.0-rc01+ raises `minSdkVersion` to 23") is correct on the dependency-floor side but the "ceiling that, if unblocked, lets activity/biometric/room/webkit lines move in lockstep" phrasing is now load-bearing for the next 6 months of dep-pin currency. Eng-Debt row updated below. | Eng-Debt row reactivates from "defer" to "decide". | [S341] |
| **AGP `8.13.2`** | Eng-Debt row claimed "Latest stable is AGP `9.2`" and "Not urgent". The 2026-05-17 release page reconfirms 9.2.0 as current stable, but also documents that **AGP 10 (late 2026) will remove all AGP-9 deprecation opt-outs**, including the explicit opt-in required to keep using deprecated DSL/Variant APIs. Pin at 8.13.2 means NG carries deprecated APIs that AGP 9 explicitly warns about and AGP 10 will refuse to load. Migration window closes well before pass-6 closeout (2026-05-17 internal target). | Eng-Debt row upgraded from `Medium / annual cycle` to `Medium-High / dated by AGP 10 GA`. | [S342] |
| **bouncycastle `1.84`** | No NG-action delta. 1.85 is **still listed `TBD`** on bcgit upstream as of 2026-05-17 and queues CVE-2026-0636 (LDAPStoreHelper LDAP injection) plus the prior triplet (3505 / 5588 / 5598) and CVE-2025-14813 (GOSTCTR). NG does **not** use `LDAPStoreHelper` (it surfaces in the bcpkix LDAP cert-store path; NG's backup-crypto only consumes `bcprov` AES/GCM and OpenPGP), so CVE-2026-0636 is informational rather than blocking. Pin and watch. | (no row change) | [S343] |

### New rows

| Item | Description | Theme | Tier |
|------|-------------|-------|------|
| **Shizuku Play Store Delisting Awareness** | Shizuku Manager was removed from Google Play for Android 16 devices on 2026-03-30; users on A16 cannot install or update Shizuku from Play, only sideload from the official GitHub releases or F-Droid/IzzyOnDroid mirror [S344]. NG's onboarding "Install Shizuku" affordance should detect the broken-Play-listing case and prefer a Play→GitHub fallback link, mirroring the pattern Obtainium ships for de-Played packages. Pairs with iter-57's OEM compatibility warning and iter-25's hidden-Shizuku-fork-detection row. Effort 2/5. | T5 | **Next** |
| **Shizuku Battery-Optimization Auto-Detect (Shizuku Manager Target)** | Multiple Shizuku tracker reports on Android 16 GDPR1 describe the **Shizuku Manager process** being killed by OEM battery / RAM managers despite the user's "disable timeout" setting; fix is granting Shizuku Manager itself the `IGNORE_BATTERY_OPTIMIZATIONS` exemption [S345]. NG already has `SelfBatteryOptimization` (iter-30) for AM's own process — extend it to detect when **Shizuku Manager** (`moe.shizuku.privileged.api`) lacks the exemption and surface a one-tap fix from Privileges / Mode Doctor when active mode is Shizuku and the binder keeps dying mid-session. Effort 2/5. | T5 | **Next** |
| **Tasker / MacroDroid Action-Provider Surface** | Tasker 6.6+ (2026-04-23) shipped first-class Shizuku integration — Tasker can now toggle system settings, disable apps, kill processes, and configure WiFi tether through a user-installed Shizuku [S346]. This creates an obvious "NG as action provider" opening: expose NG's existing iter-39 signature-protected `AutomationReceiver` actions (FREEZE / UNFREEZE / BACKUP / RESTORE / PROFILE_APPLY / INSTALL) as a **Tasker plugin** (via the `com.twofortyfouram.locale.intent` plugin API) AND a MacroDroid action set, so power-users can chain NG operations into Tasker / MacroDroid macros without re-doing the privilege handshake. Already documented in [`docs/intent-api.md`](docs/intent-api.md); pairs with the parked iter-22 Tasker row [S143]. Effort 3/5. | T8 | **Next** |
| **A16 Signature-Permission Allowlist Diagnostic** | Android 16 (and 16 QPR2) tightened the signature/privileged permission grant model: platform-signature permissions requested by non-system or updated-system apps now require explicit allowlist entries in `/etc/permissions/<name>.xml` under `<allow-permission>` blocks [S347]. NG's App Details permissions tab currently shows these permissions as denied with no explanation; users hit a wall figuring out **why** a signature perm is denied. Add a "denied — requires allowlist" diagnostic that explains the platform's allowlist requirement and links to the `/etc/permissions` doc on AOSP. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Health Connect Synthetic-Package-Name (SPN) Resolver** | Health Connect's on-device steps source moves from the generic `android` synthetic package name to a device-specific SPN in June 2026 [S348]; new Health Connect FHIR / medical-record APIs add a permission surface AM should categorize separately from fitness perms [S349]. NG's permission inspector should resolve SPNs to friendly labels (already partially done for `android`) and group Health Connect medical-data permissions distinctly from `BODY_SENSORS`. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Hidden-App Enumeration Robustness** | SD Maid SE 1.7.3-rc0 (2026-05-16) added graceful handling when the system hides installed apps from the package manager — relevant to NG's "hidden / work-profile / private-space" enumeration paths [S350]. NG's existing iter-31 cross-user package state code uses `MATCH_UNINSTALLED_PACKAGES`; private-space (Android 15+) apps are **not** included by default and currently disappear from the main list. Audit `Users.getUsersIds()` + `MainViewModel` filter chain to detect Android 15+ private-space user IDs and surface them with a distinct chip. Effort 3/5. | T5 | **Next** |
| **Service-Connection-Loss Graceful Recovery** | SD Maid SE 1.7.3-rc0 shipped fixes for service-connection-loss crashes plus dashboard recovery when the privileged service binder dies mid-screen [S350]. NG already has iter-23's privileged-batch journal + Shizuku binder-death listener (`BatchOpsJournal.markInterrupted`) for batch operations, but **single-operation screens** (App Details, Permission Inspector, Finder) currently silently fail with an opaque toast when Shizuku dies mid-call. Audit the half-dozen direct privileged-call sites and add a uniform "service connection lost — re-bind?" recovery surface. Pairs with iter-23's Shizuku binder-death watch and iter-45's audit log. Effort 3/5. | T3 / T5 | **Next** |
| **Cert-Pinning for Debloat-Definitions Manifest Fetch** | Obtainium issue #2916 (2026-05-09) requests certificate pinning for update sources, motivated by user concern about silently-rotated TLS certificates on third-party mirrors [S351]. NG's iter-32 `DebloatDefinitionsUpdater` fetches from a single pinned `raw.githubusercontent.com` URL with default platform trust store. Add an optional cert-pin (SHA-256 of GitHub's leaf or intermediate cert as of pin-time, plus a configurable backup pin) and surface a clear failure on pin mismatch instead of a generic "fetch failed". Defers to platform pinning APIs (`NetworkSecurityConfig` `<pin-set>` element) so the pin lives in `network_security_config.xml`, not in Java code. Pairs with future "Multi-Mirror Debloat-Defs Fetcher" row. Effort 2/5. | T9 | **Next** |
| **Installer-Cancel-Actually-Cancels Audit** | Inure build107.0.2 (2026-05-10) shipped a specific fix for installer-cancel-button-not-cancelling — a recurring bug class across this category [S352]. NG's `PackageInstallerActivity` / `PackageInstallerService` honor user-cancel for the *staging* phase, but during `PackageInstaller.Session.commit()` the cancel path is racy: `PackageInstallerCompat.abandon()` may be called after `commit()` has already begun, leaving the user staring at a no-op cancel button. Audit the cancel handler to confirm it produces a deterministic state (rejected / committed) and surfaces the outcome in the install transcript. Effort 2/5. | T3 | **Next** |
| **A16 Archived APK Format Recognition** | Android 16 introduced a synthetic archived-APK format (Esper deep-dive [S353]); when the system archives an app, `PackageManager.getInstalledApplications()` returns a stub `ApplicationInfo` with `category` = `CATEGORY_UNDEFINED` and an `isArchived` bit (API 35+ `ApplicationInfo.isArchived`). NG's App Details and main list currently show archived apps as "installed" with no indication, and the data tab shows zero bytes with no context. Add an "Archived" chip on archived rows and an App Details note explaining how to unarchive. Pairs with iter-31 cross-user state buckets. Effort 2/5. | T5 | **Later** |
| **A16 Bluetooth Bond-Loss / Encryption-Change Broadcast Inspector** | Android 16 added two new system intents (`ACTION_KEY_MISSING` / bond-lost + `ACTION_ENCRYPTION_CHANGE`) that the app-component receiver inspector should recognize and label [S354]. Trivial copy/icon addition to the receiver tab's known-intent table. Effort 1/5. | T9 | **Later** |
| **OEM Uninstall-Path Matrix** | Canta and UAD-NG users report consistent failure to uninstall `OplusForbidUninstallAppManager`-guarded and MIUI `com.miui.core`-guarded packages even with Shizuku [S355]; iter-23 already noted the OEM enforcement layer pattern via [S154]. Build a documented matrix of OEM (manufacturer / Android version / privilege path) → expected `pm uninstall --user 0` outcome, then surface the matrix in Debloater's confirmation dialog when the active OEM is known to block the target package. Avoids the silent "uninstalled? — actually no" UX trap. Effort 3/5. | T15 | **Later** |
| **JobScheduler / Alarm / Wake-Lock Read-Only Inspector** | Android Studio's Background Task Inspector uses `dumpsys jobscheduler`, `dumpsys alarm`, and `dumpsys power` under the hood [S356] — a Shizuku-elevated dumpsys parse can give on-device read-only parity (which Background Task Inspector lacks because it requires USB+ADB+adb-debug build). New tab under App Details (or its own Settings entry) listing the target app's scheduled jobs, pending alarms, and held wake locks with parsed reasons. Read-only; no privileged write surface. Effort 4/5. | T11 | **Later** |
| ~~**Hide-Shizuku Detection Awareness**~~ ✅ shipped 2026-05-17 (iter-67) | New `ShizukuBridge.getDisplayVersion(Context)` falls back to the binder-reported API version with a `(hidden)` suffix (e.g. `api 14 (hidden)`) when the Shizuku Manager package is hidden from `PackageManager` queries (the v13.6.0+ "Hide Shizuku" feature only removes package visibility — the binder remains reachable for authorized callers). `PrivilegeHealthPreferences` switched to use the new helper so a Hide-Shizuku-enabled install no longer reports as "unknown version" in the health screen. Pure-JVM coverage: three cases in `ShizukuBridgeTest` (installed-version-preferred, binder-fallback-when-hidden, null-when-truly-absent). Reference: [S357]. | T5 | **Eng-Debt (shipped)** |
| ~~**InstallerX-Pattern BackHandler → NavigationBackHandler Audit**~~ ✅ closed 2026-05-17 (iter-73, audit-clean) | InstallerX-Revived's fix replaced Compose's `BackHandler` with `NavigationBackHandler` — a Compose-Navigation construct. AppManagerNG is Views-based throughout. Audit of `PackageInstallerActivity` and `BatchOpsResultsActivity` shows neither overrides `onBackPressed` nor registers an `OnBackPressedDispatcher` callback — they finish via explicit `finish()` calls from button handlers / dialog dismissals, which means Android's default back-key behavior produces the standard predictive-back animation correctly. No regression equivalent to the InstallerX-Revived case applies. Eng-Debt row closed N/A. Reference: [S358]. | T2 | **Eng-Debt (closed N/A)** |
| ~~**biometric `1.4.0-alpha04` Call-Site Pre-Flight for AuthenticationResultCallback Rename**~~ ✅ closed 2026-05-17 (iter-72, audit-clean) | The 1.4.0-alpha05 (2025-12-17) rename of `onAuthFailure` → `onAuthAttemptFailed` affects `AuthenticationResultCallback` (the newer activity-result-pattern callback). AppManagerNG uses the long-standing `BiometricPrompt.AuthenticationCallback` interface (`onAuthenticationError` / `onAuthenticationSucceeded` / `onAuthenticationFailed(void)`) which is unchanged across the 1.4.0-alpha line. Verified via grep across `app/src/main/java`: zero `AuthenticationResultCallback` occurrences. The minSdk-21 → 23 cliff in alpha05 still applies if the floor lifts, but no call-site rename is required. Eng-Debt row closed as N/A. Reference: [S359]. | All | **Eng-Debt (closed N/A)** |

### Rejected (iter-63)

| Item | Reason |
|------|--------|
| **Embedded / Scoped Shizuku (Code-on-the-Go pattern)** | Some apps (e.g. the Code on the Go IDE highlighted on HN [S360]) ship a forked/scoped Shizuku embedded inside their own APK rather than depending on a user-installed Shizuku. **WONTFIX for NG.** The security model requires Shizuku to be a separate, user-authorized binder — embedding it inside a package manager creates a confused-deputy attack surface where any Shizuku-relayed call could be misattributed to NG's package identity, and the user loses the ability to revoke privilege at the Shizuku Manager level without uninstalling AppManagerNG. NG already detects "Hidden Shizuku" forks (iter-25 row) — that's the correct integration surface, not embedding. |
| **ShizuWall-Pattern Native Per-App Firewall** | ShizuWall v4.5 (2026-05-06) [S361] now offers a composite Hybrid policy combinator and screen-lock-mode netblock. **WONTFIX for NG.** Firewall is explicitly not planned per the existing T9 design — NG already cites ShizuWall and de1984 as the canonical complements ([S156], [S157]). Re-implementing a per-app firewall in NG would (a) duplicate maintenance of NetworkPolicy/`VpnService` paths that ShizuWall already handles, (b) compete with rather than complement the recommended Shizuku-ecosystem tools, and (c) violate the "complement, not replicate" rule applied to Aurora / F-Droid (see existing Rejected row "Full on-device app store"). |

### Iter-100 Closures (2026-05-18)

| Item | Result |
|------|--------|
| **Material Files User-Trust for Self-Signed WebDAV Certs** | Closed as covered by the provider-backed destination architecture from iter-99. AppManagerNG does not own WebDAV TLS handshakes when the backup destination is a user-selected `DocumentsProvider`; Material Files, DAVx5, FolderSync, or the chosen provider handles self-signed certificate and user-installed CA trust. A native `KeyChain.getCertificateChain()` trust hook remains a requirement for the later native WebDAV/provider rows if NG adds first-party protocol clients. |

### Iter-99 Closures (2026-05-18)

| Item | Result |
|------|--------|
| **SMB / WebDAV Network Backup Destination** | Closed the storage-selection slice by adding a dedicated Network backup destination action in Settings -> Backup/Restore. The action uses Android's SAF `DocumentsProvider` contract, persists read/write access to the selected tree, normalizes the tree/document URI with `StorageUtils.getFixedTreeUri`, and immediately sets it as the active backup volume. |

### Iter-98 Closures (2026-05-18)

|------|--------|

Imported selections immediately surface through the existing multi-select batch actions instead of adding a second batch-operation path. |

API-37 `JobDebugInfo` stats remain blocked until NG raises compile SDK beyond 36. |

### Iter-89 Closures (2026-05-17)

### Iter-88 Closures (2026-05-17)

| Item | Result |
|------|--------|
| **Multi-Mirror Debloat-Defs Fetcher** | Audited and parked as `Blocked` on deployment, not code. Source-side prerequisites (byte-length + SHA-256 + schema validation, single-call host allowlist via `isApprovedRawGithubUrl`) are already in place from iter-32. The blocker is operational: a secondary mirror has to exist before the multi-mirror loop has a real second URL to try; adding one today would either hallucinate a Codeberg endpoint or ship a single-entry list pretending to be multi-mirror. The signed-manifest half is a separate eng-debt item requiring a public-key-in-app + maintainer-signing pipeline. Park until either a mirror is set up or the signing infrastructure lands. |

### Iter-86 Closures (2026-05-17)

| Item | Result |
|------|--------|
| **URI / Intent Automation API** | Audited and closed as partially-shipped: (1) `am://app/<pkg>?user=<id>` deep-link shipped iter-22 via `SelfUriManager` (canonical form `app-manager://details?id=<pkg>&user=<id>`, documented in `docs/intent-api.md`); (2) operation triggers from external apps shipped iter-39 via `AutomationReceiver` under a signature-protected custom permission (FREEZE / UNFREEZE / BACKUP / RESTORE / PROFILE_APPLY / INSTALL). Row closed as partially-shipped; the unimplemented tail is documented. |
